The Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools is a body politic and corporate charged with the public duty of providing an adequate public school system for children residing in the Kinston Graded School District, a political subdivision of the State. The boundaries of this school district are practically conterminable with those of the City of Kinston, a municipal corporation of Lenoir County.

The Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools is the owner in fee simple of a tract of land situated near the Kinston High School in the City of Kinston, which it bought in 1937 from Mrs. Sadie Grainger Pierce for $ 8,500. For convenience of narration this land is hereafter called the Pierce property. The Board of Trustees purchased this property for an athletic field and playground for the children attending the Kinston Graded Schools. Ever since its acquisition, it has been used for such purpose. But during these times, the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools has been, and still is, without funds with which to construct on this land an [***2] athletic stadium required to meet the reasonable athletic and recreational needs of the Kinston Graded Schools. Consequently, the property is virtually unimproved. It will not be expedient for some years for the Kinston Graded Schools to undertake to borrow money for the erection of the needed stadium because "such course would hamper the construction of necessary additional school buildings."

The General Assembly of 1947 enacted two statutes bearing directly upon the matter in controversy. By chapter 397 of the Session Laws of 1947, the Legislature authorized the City of Kinston to erect and maintain an athletic stadium "upon lands owned by it and forming a part of its system of public parks," and to issue its bonds in a principal amount not exceeding $ 150,000 to defray the cost of constructing such stadium, and to levy a tax for paying the principal and interest on such bonds, in case such action on its part was first "approved by a majority of the qualified voters of the City of Kinston at a special election" called by its Council. By chapter 544 of the Session Laws of 1947, the General Assembly empowered the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools to convey the Pierce [***3] property to the City of Kinston in fee simple and without monetary consideration as "a part of the system of parks of the City of Kinston" and as the site for the projected athletic stadium in the event the proposal to issue bonds for the erection of the stadium was first approved by the qualified voters of the City of Kinston at the special election held under chapter 397 of the Session Laws of 1947, and in the further event that a written agreement was first entered into between the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools and the City of Kinston making the athletic stadium and the Pierce land available without charge "for all reasonable use by the Kinston Graded Schools for athletic and recreational purposes."

On 28 October, 1947, the special election was conducted in the City of Kinston in conformity to chapter 397 of the Session Laws of 1947. At this election, an overwhelming majority of the qualified voters of the City of Kinston cast their ballots in favor of the proposition to authorize the City of Kinston to erect and maintain an athletic stadium "upon lands owned by it and forming a part of its system of public parks," and to issue its bonds in a principal amount [***4] not exceeding $ 150,000 to defray the cost of erecting such stadium, and to levy a tax for paying the principal and interest on such bonds.

After the result of the special election had been duly determined and declared, the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools and the City of Kinston undertook to carry out a written agreement made by them in pursuance of the provisions of chapter 544 of the Session Laws of 1947 to effectuate the statutory purpose of making the contemplated stadium and the Pierce property available without charge "for all reasonable use by the Kinston Graded Schools for athletic and recreational purposes." By this contract, the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools bound itself to convey the Pierce land to the City of Kinston in fee simple and without monetary consideration to the end that it might become a part of the system of public parks of the City of Kinston and to the further end that it might be used as the site of the proposed athletic stadium. The City of Kinston obligated itself by this agreement to build and maintain the projected stadium on the Pierce property at its own expense, and to permit the Kinston Graded Schools to use such [***5] stadium and its site "without rent or other charge therefor, during the time from the beginning until the end of each respective school term, for athletic, instructional, and recreational purposes, when such use shall not conflict or interfere with regularly scheduled games of professional baseball played in connection with the activities of a professional baseball association holding a lease upon said stadium and grounds" from the City of Kinston. The City of Kinston further bound itself by its contract with the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools to reconvey the Pierce land to such Board of Trustees in fee simple and without monetary consideration in case the proposed stadium is destroyed by fire or other casualty and the City of Kinston fails for a period of five years to make a new stadium "available for the use of the Kinston Graded Schools as provided in this agreement."

W. E. Boney, a taxpaying resident of the City of Kinston and of the Kinston Graded School District, brought this action against the Board of Trustees of the Kinston Graded Schools, the City of Kinston, the Board of Aldermen of the City of Kinston, and Guy Elliott, the Mayor of the City of Kinston,  [***6] alleging that the written agreement between the city and the school trustees is void in law because chapter 544 of the Session Laws of 1947 contravenes Article IX, Section 5, of the North Carolina Constitution, and asking a perpetual injunction against the defendants to prevent the proposed conveyance of the Pierce property to the City of Kinston and to prevent the City of Kinston from constructing the contemplated athletic stadium on such property.

Upon application of the plaintiff, a temporary restraining order was issued, and a notice to show cause why an injunction should not be granted as prayed was served on the defendants. On the return day, Judge Stevens heard the testimony of the parties, found that the right of the Kinston Graded Schools to use the proposed stadium without charge constituted "full and adequate value for the conveyance of the land," concluded that chapter 544 of the Session Laws of 1947 is a valid exercise of legislative power, and rendered judgment dissolving the restraining order and dismissing the action. The plaintiff thereupon appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Lenoir County (North Carolina), which dissolved a temporary restraining order and dismissed his action against defendants, a city, municipal officials, and educational officials, seeking to prevent the proposed conveyance of school district property to the city.


OVERVIEW: 1947 N.C. Sess. Laws ch. 397 authorized the city to erect and maintain an athletic stadium upon lands owned by it and forming a part of its system of public parks, and to issue its bonds to defray the cost of constructing such stadium, and to levy a tax for paying the principal and interest on such bonds. 1947 N.C. Sess. Laws ch. 544 the school district was allowed to convey a parcel of its land to the city in fee simple and without monetary consideration for the site of the athletic stadium if the bond issue passed. The taxpayer alleged that the agreement between the city and the school district was void because 1947 N.C. Sess. Laws ch. 544 violated N.C. Const. art. IX, § 5, by permitting school property to be diverted from its intended use to other objects. On appeal from the judgment dismissing his action, the court affirmed. The conveyance divested the school district of legal title to the property, but it would not result in any substantial diversion of the land from its intended use. The schools were exchanging a practically unimproved tract of land for the right to the substantial use of a stadium. The conveyance was based upon a valuable consideration.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the taxpayer's action challenging the sale of the school property to the city was affirmed.

 

849 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Coble v. Coble


No. 675


Supreme Court of North Carolina


229 N.C. 81; 47 S.E.2d 798; 1948 N.C. LEXIS 429



May 19, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from Armstrong, J., at Chambers, in Greensboro, N. C., 18 March, 1948, Guilford.

Civil action for divorce on the grounds of adultery and for the custody of the children born of the marriage, heard upon special appearance and motion to vacate an order awarding the custody of the children to plaintiff.

Plaintiff and defendant are man and wife, living in a state of separation. On 9 December 1947, plaintiff instituted a proceeding in the juvenile court of Greensboro for the purpose of obtaining custody of the two children born of the marriage. As notice of the hearing thereon could not be served on defendant, the proceeding was dismissed on motion of plaintiff.

The plaintiff then, on 26 January 1948, instituted this action. The summons was returned 27 January, unserved for the reason defendant could not be found in Guilford County. Thereupon, the court, upon motion of plaintiff, entered an order committing the custody of said children to plaintiff. This order was likewise returned unserved.

Complaint was filed 26 January in which plaintiff alleges, in respect to the proceedings in the juvenile court, "that the defendant removed said minor children and [***2] herself from the State of North Carolina and beyond the jurisdiction of this Court for the purpose of escaping the jurisdiction of the courts of North Carolina and to avoid the service of lawful process upon her; that, process having failed, said proceedings in the Juvenile Court were, at the request of the petitioner therein (the plaintiff herein) dismissed."

Order for the service of summons by publication was duly entered 30 January and service thereof was duly made by publication as required by law.

On 14 February, defendant, through counsel, entered a special appearance and moved the court to vacate and set aside the order awarding custody of the children to plaintiff and directing defendant to surrender custody thereof immediately to the plaintiff.

On 15 March, between the date the motion was made and the hearing thereon, plaintiff, in some undisclosed manner, acquired custody and possession of his children near Greenville, S. C.

On 18 March, the court below, after hearing, denied the motion to vacate and defendant excepted and appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife challenged an order of the trial court (North Carolina) denying her motion to vacate the award of custody of her and plaintiff husband's children to the husband in an action for divorce and child custody brought by the husband.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife were married and had children. The husband brought an action for divorce and custody of the children, and the trial court awarded custody of the children to the husband. The wife sought review, and the court reversed. The court held that child custody and divorce proceedings were in rem actions and that the children and the status of the marriage were the res of the actions. The wife and the children were beyond the jurisdiction of the court when the award of custody was made; therefore, the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the res of the action. The court had no power to issue orders involving people not within its jurisdiction because notice and an opportunity to be heard were requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the wife's motion to vacate the order awarding custody of the children to the husband.

 

850 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Pridgen v. Carolina Coach Co.


No. 455


Supreme Court of North Carolina


229 N.C. 46; 47 S.E.2d 609; 1948 N.C. LEXIS 417



May 5, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff from Grady, Emergency Judge, at the January Term, 1948, of Wake.

This is a civil action for false imprisonment and malicious prosecution.

On 28 September, 1946, the plaintiff purchased a ticket from a ticket agent at the Raleigh Union Bus Depot, for transportation from Raleigh, N. C., to Norfolk, Va. The ticket was sold subject to the rules and regulations of the defendant carrier. The plaintiff boarded one of the buses operated by the defendant, which was scheduled to leave immediately for Norfolk. Upon entering the bus, he took a seat at or near the middle of the bus. The driver of the bus requested the plaintiff to move to the rear, stating to him that he being a Negro, the rules and regulations of the company and the law of the State of North Carolina required him to sit in the back of the bus. The bus was crowded; white people were sitting behind the plaintiff, and the only vacant seats were in the rear. Plaintiff refused to move, on the ground that he was an interstate passenger, and was not amenable to such rules or to the law of North Carolina, requiring segregation of passengers on the basis of race, in vehicles of public carriage. Whereupon,  [***2] the driver called one W. A. Green, a dispatcher for the defendant, who likewise requested the plaintiff to move to the rear of the bus. The plaintiff again refused to move. Mr. Green requested him to get off the bus if he would not move to the rear as requested; he refused to do so. Mr. Green then got off the bus and sent Sgt. W. J. Horton, a Raleigh policeman, on the bus. Sgt. Horton requested plaintiff to sit in the back of the bus. The plaintiff stated to him that he was an interstate passenger and held a ticket to Norfolk, Va., and was within his rights to sit in any available space during interstate travel, and Sgt. Horton left. He re-entered the bus later and told plaintiff that he was under arrest. Both the driver and Mr. Green were present at the time the plaintiff was arrested. Sgt. Horton and Mr. Green informed the plaintiff he could get back on the bus if he would sit in the rear. He refused to go back, and the bus left. The plaintiff, according to his evidence, was treated courteously by Mr. Green and the bus driver. He also testified that he was thoroughly "versed with all the rules and regulations of the company," and knew if he did not comply with them he [***3] was subject to removal.

After the Norfolk bus left, Mr. Green accompanied the plaintiff and the officer to the City Hall, where Mr. Green signed a warrant charging the plaintiff with disorderly conduct for refusing to comply with the rules and regulations of the Carolina Coach Company, as ordered by its driver, A. F. Collier. The plaintiff was released on bond. When the case was called for trial, no one appeared as a witness against the plaintiff, and the State took a nolle prosequi.

At the close of plaintiff's evidence the court held the warrant signed by Mr. Green did not charge a crime, and was void; therefore the plaintiff had no cause of action for malicious prosecution. Young v. Hardwood Co., 200 N. C., 310, 156 S. E., 501. No exception was taken to this ruling.

The defendant then moved for judgment as of nonsuit, and the motion was allowed on the ground that the evidence is insufficient to show that the defendant was responsible for plaintiff's arrest. Judgment was entered accordingly, and the plaintiff appealed, assigning error.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger appealed a decision of a Wake County trial court (North Carolina), which found in favor of defendant bus company on the passenger's action for false imprisonment and malicious prosecution.


OVERVIEW: The passenger, an African-American, was ordered by the bus driver to move from his seat in the middle of the bus and to sit in the rear. The passenger refused to move and he was then arrested by a police officer. When the case was called for trial, no one appeared as a witness against the passenger, and the State took a nolle prosequi. On appeal from the judgment in favor of the bus company on the passenger's action for false imprisonment, the court affirmed, holding that removal from the bus did not constitute false imprisonment as long as he was free to re-enter the bus and proceed on his journey, provided he would abide by the rules and regulations of the company. The dispatcher who called the police was not acting within the scope of his authority when he left the premises and obtained a warrant for the arrest of the passenger. The bus company did not authorize or ratify that action.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the bus company on the passenger's action for false imprisonment and malicious prosecution was affirmed.

 

851 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Glidden Co.


No. 293


Supreme Court of North Carolina


228 N.C. 664; 46 S.E.2d 860; 1948 N.C. LEXIS 313



March 24, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] State's appeal from Gwyn, J., November Term, 1947, Caldwell Superior Court.

This cause was begun by warrant in the recorder's court of Caldwell County and reached the Superior Court of that county on appeal of the defendant from conviction and fine of $ 5,000, suspended on condition that defendant, after the 15th day of December, 1947, desist from discharging into the streams and waters of the State, "any substance created from its mining operations."

The warrant was amended in Superior Court by inserting therein the statement that defendant was "a corporation duly chartered on or after the 4th day of March, 1915."

When the case came on for a hearing the defendant, before pleading, demurred to the warrant as not charging a criminal offense, for that the statute on which it is based, to wit: G. S., 113-172, is in violation of Article I, Section 7, of the State Constitution in attempting to confer exclusive or separate emoluments or privileges not in consideration of public services, and Article I, Section 17, guaranteeing due process of law in protection of life, liberty and property. The statute reads as follows:

"It shall be unlawful to discharge or to cause or permit [***2] to be discharged into the waters of the state any deleterious or poisonous substance or substances inimical to the fishes inhabiting the said water; and any person, persons or corporation violating the provisions of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, be fined or imprisoned in the discretion of the court: Provided, this section shall not apply to corporations chartered either by general law or special act before the 4th day of March, 1915. (1915, c. 84, s. 20; C. S., 1899.)"


Upon inspection of the warrant, the court, being of the opinion that the statute under which it is brought violates the Constitution in the respects pleaded, sustained the demurrer and dismissed the action. The State appealed. G. S., 15-179.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the Caldwell County Superior Court (North Carolina) that dismissed an action against defendant, a corporation, for violating N.C. Gen. Stat. § 113-172. The statute prohibited the discharge of poisonous or deleterious substances into streams. Following an appeal of a conviction from the recorder's court, the superior court dismissed on the ground that § 113-172 violated N.C. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 17.


OVERVIEW: Section 113-172 included an exemption for all corporations chartered before March 4, 1915. Defendant was not exempt from prosecution under the statute and demurred to a warrant charging it with violating the statute. The superior court held that the statute violated the North Carolina Constitution and the court on appeal affirmed. Class legislation was not unconstitutional per se as long as there were reasonable grounds for the classification and if persons in the same classification were treated with uniformity. If a criminal statute depended on an arbitrary or unreasonable distinction between similarly situated persons, the statute violated principles of equal protection. The distinction between corporations based on their date of incorporation, irrespective of whether they were or were not engaged in acts of pollution, was not a reasonable distinction and was unrelated to the purpose of the statute. Therefore, the court held that the statute was void for contravening the equal protection guarantee. The court also held that the statute did no violate due process rights and that defendant had a right to contest the validity of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

In re Wright


No. 593


Supreme Court of North Carolina


228 N.C. 584; 46 S.E.2d 696; 1948 N.C. LEXIS 285



March 17, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to rehear.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the North Carolina Department of Motor Vehicles, filed a petition for rehearing of a judgment, which affirmed a trial court's reversal of the Department's revocation or suspension of the driver's license of appellee driver pursuant to G. S. 20-23.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was revoked based upon an offense that he committed in another state. The Department claimed, inter alia, that the court erred in that it interpreted and applied G. S. 20-16, whereas the driver's license was revoked under the terms of G. S. 20-23, that court had no jurisdiction to review Department's revocation of the license under G. S. 20-23, and that G. S. 20-25, as interpreted by the court, was unconstitutional. The court ruled, inter alia, that (1) G. S. 20-16 and G. S. 20-23 were parts of the same statute and related to the same subject matter, and thus they had to be considered in pari materia; (2) G. S. 20-16(7) was the real source of authority for suspension, and G. S. 20-23 prescribed a rule of evidence and added the power of revocation when G. S. 20-16(7) was the basis of action; (3) the court's authority under G. S. 20-25 to review the Department's discretionary suspensions and revocations did not constitute a delegation of legislative and administrative authority; and (4) the driver's license was not subject to suspension or revocation, and he was entitled to a hearing in the trial court, even though the Department acted under G. S. 20-23.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Department's petition.

Winborne v. Easley

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from an order of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) invalidating portions of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 163-278.13B that barred campaign contributions by political action committees because it restricted political free speech in violation of U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV.

The appellate court affirmed the order, holding that the issue was properly before the trial court and it did not err by finding the statute was not narrowly drawn to serve the compelling governmental interest of preventing corruption or the appearance of corruption.

OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed; the trial court correctly dismissed plaintiff's complaint because the drug tax did not constitute a criminal penalty, and therefore plaintiff was not entitled to the procedural safeguards required for criminal proceedings.

State v. Chisholm


NO. COA98-1302


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


135 N.C. App. 578; 521 S.E.2d 487; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 1182


August 26, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 16, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the State of North Carolina and Carteret County from judgment entered 18 September 1998 by Judge Paul Quinn in District Court, Carteret County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed the judgment of the District Court, Carteret County (North Carolina), holding that the state's impaired driving and license revocation laws were unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. IV, V, and XIV, and N.C. Const. art. I, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state appealed holding that North Carolina's impaired driving and license revocation laws were unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. IV, V, and XIV, and N.C. Const. art. I, § 19. Appellee vehicle owner argued the appeal was moot due to changes in the laws. However, the court disagreed, finding the decision could impact other vehicle owners. The court found there was probable cause for arresting appellee and seizing his vehicle and, therefore, the seizure was constitutional. The court held there was no equal protection violation because the statutes applied equally to all persons whose vehicles were used in an illegal manner, they had the legitimate objective of keeping impaired drivers and their cars off the roads, and seizure was directly related to that goal. The court determined that the laws had a legitimate objective that was reasonably implemented; thus, they were constitutional under N.C. Const. art. I, § 19.


OUTCOME: The district court's holding that the impaired driving and license revocation laws were unconstitutional was reversed because law enforcement had probable cause to seize appellee's vehicle, the statutes applied equally to all persons, and the statutes had a reasonably implemented legitimate objective.

State v. Thomas


NO. COA98-715


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


134 N.C. App. 560; 518 S.E.2d 222; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 857


March 17, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 17, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 10 December 1997 by Judge Cy A. Grant in Nash County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Nash County Superior Court (North Carolina), which entered a conviction of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: During his trial for first-degree murder, defendant proceeded pro se and was appointed standby counsel. Plaintiff state presented several witnesses and substantial evidence supporting its position. Defendant did not present any evidence in his defense. The trial court found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed, claiming that he was prejudiced because he remained shackled, and that standby counsel's participation constituted impermissible "hybrid" representation. In addition, defendant asserted that plaintiff lacked sufficient evidence to conclude that defendant was the perpetrator of the crime. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, reasoning that defendant waived his right to argue prejudice due to his being shackled, because he failed to object during the trial proceedings. Moreover, the record reflected that standby counsel only participated when instructed by defendant, and did not interfere with defendant's right to self-representation. Lastly, the court reasoned that defendant had a fair trial and was not prejudiced by the evidence admitted or the behavior of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court which convicted defendant of first-degree murder was affirmed, because defendant was afforded a fair trial and the trial court did not prejudice defendant by admitting evidence, allowing standby counsel's participation, or having defendant shackled during trial.

Shell Island Homeowners Ass'n v. Tomlinson


NO. COA98-961


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


134 N.C. App. 217; 517 S.E.2d 406; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 751


May 11, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiffs from order entered 14 July 1998 by Judge James D. Llewellyn in New Hanover County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff unit owners appealed from order of New Hanover County Superior Court (North Carolina), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss and affirmed the denial of plaintiffs' construction permits and enforcement of its hardened structure rule regulations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought permits to construct various hardened erosion control structures to protect its resort from erosion. Defendants enforced the hardened structure rule and denied the applications and refused plaintiffs' requests for variances. Plaintiffs had not sought administrative review of any of defendants' decisions enforcing the hardened structure rules, and they had not applied for a permit for a permanent erosion control structure since their application for a variance was originally denied. Instead, plaintiffs filed suit. Defendants moved to dismiss plaintiff's complaint for lack of standing and failure to state a claim and the trial court granted the motion. Plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed and held that plaintiffs failed to pursue their administrative remedies before filing suit and lacked standing to sue. Plaintiffs were also estopped from claiming that the rules were invalid when they used the variance granted pursuant to those rules. Also, plaintiffs were unable to show loss of all economic value for their takings claim and the rules were in effect when they bought the land and therefore were made part of the title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of plaintiffs' action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because plaintiffs failed to exhaust the administrative remedies of the non-constitutional claims contained in their complaint and they failed to show that the constitutional protections on their claims of due process, equal protection, and taking of property applied to them.

Shell Island Homeowners Ass'n v. Tomlinson

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

July 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 12 August 1998 by Judge James D. Llewellyn in New Hanover County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners association appealed from an order of the New Hanover County Superior Court (North Carolina), which dismissed its claim alleging denial by defendant state agencies and official of its requests to build erosion control structures was a taking of its property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff homeowners association claimed that denial by defendant state agencies and official of plaintiff's requests to build erosion control structures was a taking of its property without just compensation. The state issued a permit in error to build a hotel, which exceeded development standards. After the hotel was built, an inlet migrated, causing shoreline erosion around plaintiff's island. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's claims. The appellate court affirmed. Plaintiff's claims were properly dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction on the grounds that they were moot. The essence of relief plaintiff sought was a determination that defendants' denials of its requests for variances were a regulatory taking. The granting of plaintiff's fourth variance request rendered moot the issues relating to earlier variance requests because it provided plaintiff with the relief originally sought. Plaintiff contended that the physical invasion by inlet waters during the time in which its variance requests were denied was a compensable taking that was not mooted. Since the issue was not before the trial court, the appellate court refused to consider it on appeal.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing claims of plaintiff homeowners association for a taking without just compensation was affirmed because the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction as all claims were moot.

Crump v. Snead


NO. COA98-1424


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


134 N.C. App. 353; 517 S.E.2d 384; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 760


June 9, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by petitioners from judgment entered 16 October 1998 by Judge Sanford L. Steelman, Jr., in Richmond County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed the Richmond County Superior Court (North Carolina) order that dismissed their petition for a declaratory judgment that legislation that amended the city charter was a violation of N.C. Const. Art. I, §§ 9, 14, 35, 36, and that respondent was not a lawful member of the city council.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought to have individual defendant removed from his seat on the city counsel. The court affirmed dismissal of their petition. N.C. Const. art. VII, § 1 did not forbid the recent amendment to the city charter which extended respondent's seat from two years to four years. As the office was not mandated by the North Carolina constitution, the North Carolina General Assembly had the authority to extend the term of the city counsel seats and to pay respondent for the added time on the term. This did not violate art. I, § 32, because the bill provided for a public purpose, was in the public interest, and did not confer exclusive emolument on the respondent. Petitioners did not have a right, but a privilege to run for office. As neither petitioner had a constitutional right infringed, there was no violation of art. I, §§ 9, 14, 35, 36.


OUTCOME: The superior court order that dismissed the petition and found the recent legislation constitutional was affirmed because the North Carolina General Assembly was acting within its authority and did not extend an exclusive emolument on respondent. Petitioners had no constitutional right to participate in the political process infringed.

Staley v. Lingerfelt


NO. COA98-1293


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the Gaston County Superior Court (North Carolina), which dismissed their claims against defendant city and all their claims against defendant police officer except for loss of consortium and violation of civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's mother was in a car accident. Defendants were the investigating police officer, both as an individual and official, and the city he worked for. Plaintiff had an altercation with the other driver. Defendant officer filed criminal charges against plaintiff. Plaintiffs sued defendants, city and the police officer for 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 violations and loss of consortium. Plaintiffs dismissed the complaint and then filed a second complaint setting forth additional claims and seeking punitive damages. The appellate court affirmed, except it allowed the punitive damages claim against defendant police officer individually and remanded. The state law claims made for the first time in the second complaint, except for punitive damages, were independent causes of action with unique elements which plaintiffs had to prove. Although the claims arose from the same events as the § 1983 and loss of consortium claims, defendants were not timely notified, and the statute of limitations barred the claims.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing claims against defendant city and defendant police officer was affirmed, except claims against defendant police officer as an individual for civil rights violations and loss of consortium could proceed, and order granting summary judgment for defendant police officer as an individual for punitive damages was reversed.

Gen. Stat. §§ 136-68 and 136-69, as amended by 1995 N.C. Session Laws ch. 513.

Respondent property owners filed motions for summary judgment, which the lower court denied and awarded summary judgment in favor of petitioner. 865 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


In re A Declaratory Ruling by the N.C. Comm'r of Ins. Regarding 11 N.C.A.C. 12.0319


NO. COA98-927


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


134 N.C. App. 22; 517 S.E.2d 134; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 665


March 30, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 6, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by North Carolina Commissioner of Insurance from judgment entered 20 April 1998 by Judge Robert L. Farmer in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state regulatory agency sought to overturn the judgment of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) favoring appellee insurance companies and declaring state anti-subrogation rule unenforceable on constitutional and nonconstitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellee insurance companies sought declaration that anti-subrogation rule was unenforceable. Appellant state regulatory agency held otherwise, but trial court held for appellees. Appellant challenged the ruling, and the court reversed. Court opined that the legislature expressly gave appellant power to regulate insurance industry and that legislative history and pronouncements indicated a legislative intent to grant appellant broad authority to limit insurance policy provisions, including subrogation, which were significantly unfavorable to the public. The court also found that the mere fact that appellant's anti-subrogation rule altered the common law was insufficient grounds to prohibit enforcement of it because agencies that were granted rule-making authority were authorized to modify the common law. Finally, the court found that the legislative grant of rule-making power was sufficiently limited to be constitutional and that the rule was not unconstitutional, either as interfering with a right to contract or as violative of equal protection, because it was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose.


OUTCOME: Judgment for appellee insurance companies was reversed. The court found that anti-subrogation rule was within legislature's broad grant of regulatory authority, that such a grant of authority was not impermissibly broad, and that there was no constitutional violation because the rule satisfied rational basis review.

In re Change of Name of Crawford to Crawford Trull


NO. COA98-1274


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


134 N.C. App. 137; 517 S.E.2d 161; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 678


May 11, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by petitioner from order entered 15 June 1998 by Judge Robert L. Farmer in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged an order form the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), in which the court denied petitioner's motion to change the minor child's name without respondent's consent pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 101-2.


OVERVIEW: The judgment denying petitioner's motion to change the minor child's surname was affirmed. In affirming the trial court's decision, the appeals court held that the court properly denied the petition where respondent did not consent to the name change. According to the appeals court, petitioner did not have the right to unilaterally change the minor child's surname where paternity was established. The appeals court held that pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 130A-101(f)(4), because the father's name was listed on the birth certificate the court must seek respondent's consent because respondent had parental rights. Hence, the appeals court held that the trial properly considered and afforded § 101-2 the proper weight. Next, the appeals court declined to decide petitioner's constitutional arguments because they were not raised in the lower court. Lastly, the appeals court held that the trial court was not required to engage in the "best interest" analysis when considering a name change under §§ 130A-101(f)(4) and 101-2.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment denying petitioner's motion to change the minor child's surname because respondent was required to consent to the name change where paternity was established and respondent's surname was listed on the birth certificate.

State v. Jones

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment of Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina), convicting him of felony murder and assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-32(b) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Two people were killed when defendant committed an assault with his automobile by driving it in a reckless manner. After he was convicted of felony murder and assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-32(b) (1993), defendant appealed. On appeal, the court noted that the felony murder rule was criticized in some jurisdictions, but concluded that it was bound by the plain language of the statute and earlier appellate decisions, and that application of the felony murder rule did not cause a fundamentally unfair result. The court affirmed conviction because no prejudicial error was committed at defendant's trial. The court disagreed with defendant's claim that application of the felony murder rule violated the ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for felony murder and assault with a deadly weapon inflicting serious injury because no prejudicial error was committed at defendant's trial and the application of the felony murder rule did not cause a fundamentally unfair result.

JWL Invs., Inc. v. Guilford County Bd. of Adjustment

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

June 1, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by petitioners from judgment entered 9 June 1998 by Judge Michael E. Beale in Guilford County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed the decision of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which held that petitioners violated a zoning use ordinance by storing vehicles on a residential lot in a scenic corridor.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners owned property subject to a scenic corridor ordinance. Petitioners were cited with a violation of the Guilford County Development Ordinance § 4-3.1 for storing vehicles in the scenic corridor. No unconstitutional taking of property occurred because petitioners were not deprived of all economically beneficial or productive use of their property. The respondent Board's findings were supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding that petitioners violated a zoning ordinance by storing vehicles on a residential lot in a scenic corridor because no unconstitutional taking of property occurred, and the decision was supported by substantial evidence.

State v. Nesbitt


NO. COA98-815


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


133 N.C. App. 420; 515 S.E.2d 503; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 509


March 30, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
June 1, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from judgments dated 29 January 1998 by Judge William Z. Wood, Jr. in Forsyth County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina), where he was convicted of six counts of taking indecent liberties with a minor child in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-202.1(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of six counts of taking indecent liberties with a minor child in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-202.1(a)(1). Defendant was seen masturbating in his home behind a sliding glass door facing the roadway near a school bus stop. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction because there was sufficient evidence to sustain the conviction. The fact that defendant was inside his home and the children were 35 feet away from defendant was not material. The court held that § 14-202.1(a)(1) was not impermissibly vague. The trial court did not err by instructing the jury that masturbation in the presence of another would be an immoral or indecent act. When a jury charge as a whole presents the law accurately, fairly, and clearly, reversible error does not occur. There was no prejudicial error in the instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of six counts of taking indecent liberties with a minor child because there was sufficient evidence to sustain the conviction, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, and the court's jury instructions were not improper.

Polygenex Int'l, Inc. v. Polyzen, Inc.


NO. COA98-908


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


133 N.C. App. 245; 515 S.E.2d 457; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 410


April 19, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 18, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 11 May 1998 by Judge Stafford G. Bullock in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed the judgment from the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina). The court imposed sanctions on plaintiff under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, Rule 11, for filing a breach of contract and trademark infringement suit that was not well-grounded in fact, not warranted by existing law, and interposed for an improper purpose. The court also imposed sanctions on a non-party corporate officer who verified the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation sued defendants for breach of contract, tortious interference with contract, and trademark infringement. Defendants moved for sanctions under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, Rule 11, arguing that the complaint was not well-grounded in fact, not warranted by existing law, and interposed for an improper purpose. The trial court sanctioned plaintiff and a non-party corporate officer who verified the complaint on behalf of plaintiff. The court vacated the order as to the corporate officer. The officer's verification of the complaint was performed in his capacity as a corporate officer, not in his individual capacity, and thus the verification was not sufficient to subject him to individual liability. Because the officer was not a party to the action and was never served with summons, he was not given the necessary notice and opportunity to be heard. The court affirmed the order as to plaintiff. Plaintiff failed to allege specific provisions of the contract that were breached. There was no evidence in the record that any of defendants' contacts with vendors caused actual damage to plaintiff, or that defendants infringed plaintiff's trademark.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and vacated and remanded in part, the judgment sanctioning plaintiff corporation and a non-party corporate officer for bringing an improper complaint. The officer was not given the necessary notice and opportunity to be heard, and thus that part of the judgment was defective. However, the trial court's finding that plaintiff corporation filed an improper complaint was supported by sufficient evidence.

Hardy v. Moore County


NO. COA98-1007


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


133 N.C. App. 321; 515 S.E.2d 84; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 416


April 1, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 18, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff from judgment entered 15 April 1998 by Judge W. Douglas Albright and filed 22 April 1998 in Moore County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order of the Moore County Superior Court (North Carolina) granting summary judgment to defendants, in plaintiff's action challenging the validity of a tax foreclosure sale conducted by defendants pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-375. Plaintiff contended that there was a question of fact whether defendants complied with the statutory requirement of "due diligence" in seeking his address to afford him notice.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a resident and citizen of the United Kingdom, owned property in Moore County, North Carolina. Plaintiff furnished his address to defendant tax department and received notices for two years. Plaintiff later moved and arranged for his mail to be forwarded, but failed to notify defendant tax department of the new address. Defendant tax department began foreclosure proceedings pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-375, after the taxes were not paid for five years. Plaintiff learned of the sale the following year and filed suit against defendants challenging the validity of the sale. Plaintiff appealed a trial court order granting summary judgment to defendants. Plaintiff contended that there was a question of fact whether defendants complied with the statutory requirement of "due diligence" in seeking his address to afford him notice. The appeals court affirmed. The court reasoned that plaintiff was aware of his responsibility to pay taxes, and requiring defendant to place a telephone call to obtain plaintiff's address would place an "intolerable burden" on local taxing units and would render N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-375 impracticable.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendants, because defendants complied with statutory notice provisions by sending tax notices to plaintiff's last known address. The court opined that plaintiff was aware of his responsibility to pay taxes and caused the problem by failing to update his address.

Union Carbide Corp. v. Offerman


NO. COA97-956


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


132 N.C. App. 665; 513 S.E.2d 341; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 256; 23 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1463



April 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Reconsidered in light of Polaroid Corp. v. Offerman, 349 N.C. 290, 507 S.E.2d 284 (1998), pursuant to 30 December 1998 order of the North Carolina Supreme Court. Originally heard in the Court of Appeals 19 March 1998.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to an order of the North Carolina Supreme Court, the court reconsidered the issue of whether pension plan reversion income of plaintiff, a New York corporation domiciled in Connecticut and qualified to do business in North Carolina, was properly classified as business income or nonbusiness income.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a New York corporation domiciled in Connecticut and doing business in North Carolina, was a chemical manufacturer. Plaintiff effected a reversion of funds by removing assets from its overfunded pension plan to purchase annuities for employee benefits. The $ 500 million remaining were used to buy the company's stock to avoid a hostile takeover. Plaintiff classified the $ 500 million as nonbusiness income under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-130.4(a)(1) (1985) and allocated the entire amount to Connecticut for taxation there. The State of North Carolina reclassified the reversionary income as business income and levied tax on the funds. Plaintiff, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267 (1986), sought a refund of taxes paid. On reconsideration pursuant to a court order, the court affirmed its prior decision, which held the reversionary income was nonbusiness income. The reversion was a rare and extraordinary event and not business income under the transactional test. The pension plan was not essential to plaintiff's manufacturing and selling chemicals, and any income derived from the management, acquisition, or disposition of it was nonbusiness income under the functional test.


OUTCOME: Decision that held plaintiff's reversionary income was nonbusiness income was affirmed because the reversion was nonbusiness income under both the transactional and functional tests.

Teleflex Info. Sys., Inc. v. Arnold


NO. COA96-1067


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


132 N.C. App. 689; 513 S.E.2d 85; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 283; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1244; 50 U.S.P.Q.2D (BNA) 1779


February 16, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
April 6, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by David J. Arnold, Jr., third-party plaintiff, from judgment entered 11 March 1996 by Judge W. Steven Allen, Sr., in Guilford County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff former employee appealed from the summary judgment of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which was entered for third-party defendant employer on claims of wrongful termination of at-will employment, breach of duty of fair dealing, and interference with prospective economic relations, in connection with his discharge for refusal to disclaim an ownership interest in a certain process he had developed.


OVERVIEW: An injunction was issued against third-party plaintiff former employee after his at-will employment was terminated when he refused to sign a document disclaiming an ownership interest in a new batch billing process he had developed. Thereafter, he brought a third-party action against third-party defendant employer for wrongful termination, breach of duty of fair dealing, and interference with prospective economic relations. Summary judgment was entered against him and he appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that third-party plaintiff failed to prove that his discharge fell within the public policy exception to the rule that at-will employment did not support an action for wrongful termination. Exceptions to the rule were not created by the Patent Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, or for his right to the fruits of his labors, under N.C. Const. art. I, § 1. Also, he was not denied access to the courts or the right to free speech. North Carolina law did not recognize his claim for wrongful discharge in bad faith and he failed to point to any prospective relationship with which third-party defendant interfered.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for third-party defendant was affirmed because third-party plaintiff's discharge did not violate public policy with respect to patents, his right to the fruit of his labors, his right to judicial access, or his free speech rights; a fair dealing claim was not applicable to at-will employment; and he failed to identify any prospective relationship with which third-party defendant interfered.

 

874 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Price v. Davis


NO. COA98-591


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


132 N.C. App. 556; 512 S.E.2d 783; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 228


January 11, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 16, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendants from order entered 6 March 1998 by Judge Cy A. Grant, Sr., in Northampton County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the Northampton County Superior Court (North Carolina) order that denied their motion for summary judgment on the grounds of sovereign and governmental immunity in their official capacity, and qualified immunity as individuals, in an action alleging violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 148-11, prison policy, and plaintiff's constitutional right to meaningful access to the courts.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought monetary recovery for having had his writing supplies confiscated following his transfer to a new prison. The court reversed denial of defendant's motion for summary judgment that was based on immunity. Summary judgment was improperly denied as to defendants' official capacities. Sovereign immunity barred plaintiff's claims for damages. Plaintiff failed to allege, and the record did not show, that immunity had been waived for the state law claims, and 42 U.S.C.S. §1983 excluded officers acting within their official capacity from its liability. Summary judgment was improperly denied as to defendants' individual capacities. Defendants' actions were objectively reasonable. They had discretion under the prison operating procedures and policy manual to confiscate items that were classified as contraband, such as solid-barrel writing instruments. Further, their acts were protected by public official immunity from individual liability for alleged violations of state statutes and prison regulations. Plaintiff failed to show that defendants acted maliciously or outside the scope of their authority, and therefore failed to show an essential element of his claim.


OUTCOME: The order that denied defendants' motion for summary judgment as to liability in their official and individual capacities was reversed, and the action remanded. Defendants retained sovereign immunity in their official capacities and official immunity in their individual capacities because plaintiff failed to show that defendants acted maliciously or outside the scope of their authority.

State v. Minor


NO. COA98-393


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


132 N.C. App. 478; 512 S.E.2d 483; 1999 N.C. App. LEXIS 190


January 6, 1999, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 2, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 30 September 1997 by Judge Ronald Stephens in Durham County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Durham County Superior Court (North Carolina) denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized following a search of defendant's person and vehicle allegedly in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a vehicle that was stopped by police officers for an illegible temporary tag. One officer saw defendant reach toward the center console and rub his thigh as though feeling in his pocket. The officer frisked defendant but did not find any contraband. There was no reply when the officers asked for consent to search the vehicle. The vehicle was searched and a gun and cocaine were found in defendant's jacket. Defendant was arrested. The vehicle's tag was valid. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence was denied and defendant entered guilty pleas to possession of a schedule II substance and carrying a concealed weapon. Defendant appealed the denial of the suppression motion. The appellate court reversed and held that the vehicle search violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV. Defendant's reaching for the center console and rubbing his thigh were not clearly furtive gestures. Therefore, the officers lacked probable cause for a warrantless search of the vehicle's passenger compartment when the officers had no other specific knowledge concerning evidence of a crime. The search of defendant's person was harmless error because no evidence was found.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized following a search of defendant's vehicle and held that police officers did not have probable cause to perform a warrantless search of the passenger compartment of the vehicle.

State v. Schiffer

OVERVIEW: The arresting officer stopped defendant's vehicle because the officer believed that the tinting on the car was darker than permitted by law. The court further held that the evidence supported the trial court's finding that consent to the search was given voluntarily.

DOT v. Rowe


NO. COA97-1470

August 27, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 20, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendants from judgment entered by Judge J. Marlene Hyatt on 17 June 1997 in Catawba County Superior Court and orders entered by Judge James L. Baker, Jr., on 8 May 1997 and 16 May 1997 in Catawba County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: New trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, owners, appealed the judgment of the Catawba County Superior Court (North Carolina) denying the owners any compensation for land which plaintiff agency condemned.


OVERVIEW: A portion of the owners' 18-acre tract was condemned by the agency. A hearing was held pursuant to the provisions of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 136-108 (1993) to determine issues other than the amount of damages. After the taking, the owners were left with four small remainder tracts of land, which totaled 6.712 acres. The trial court determined that the owners' remaining four small tracts, which were not condemned by the agency, had physical unity, and therefore, they were affected by the taking. At trial, the owners were found to not be entitled to any compensation for the taking because of the increase in value of the remaining tracts which was offset against any loss suffered by the taking. The appellate court awarded a new trial. The trial court abused its discretion in preventing the agency's witness from giving his opinion, during the owners' cross-examination of the witness, as to the pre-taking value of a 4.753-acre tract that was condemned for the same project. The size of the tract was only one factor for the trial court to consider in exercising its discretion in admitting the evidence of the sale price of comparable property.


OUTCOME: A new trial was awarded.

Jackson v. North Carolina Dep't of Human Resources Div. of Mental Health, Developmental Disabilities, & Substance Abuse Servs.


NO. COA97-1169


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


131 N.C. App. 179; 505 S.E.2d 899; 1998 N.C. App. LEXIS 1306


April 30, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 20, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 22 April 1997 by Judge Robert H. Hobgood in Orange County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, appointed guardian ad litem for her minor son (guardian), sought monetary damages as well as injunctive and declaratory relief against defendants, state agency and area authority. The state agency and area authority filed motions to dismiss, which the Orange County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted, dismissing the complaint without prejudice for the guardian's failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the area authority refused payment for the minor son's hospitalization, the guardian filed suit. On appeal, the guardian argued that the appeals procedures were improperly promulgated and published, and thus the trial court erred in requiring her to exhaust administrative remedies. The court held that the provisions of the North Carolina Administrative Procedure Act (NCAPA), N.C. Gen. Stat. § 150B-1 et seq., applied to the area authority and the state agency. The court note that, as here, where no administrative remedies were promulgated, the NCAPA itself provided the procedures for administrative review. The court held that NCAPA provided adequate remedies for the minor son; he became an aggrieved person when he was denied medical care, and as such was entitled to an administrative hearing to appeal that denial. The guardian's mere allegations that administrative remedies were inadequate and her inclusion of a request for injunctive relief were insufficient to excuse her from the exhaustion requirement. The court held that the issue of whether the minor son was improperly denied care should be determined by the agencies statutorily charged with administering that care.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of dismissal without prejudice of the guardian's complaint.

 

881 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Blackmon


NO. COA97-326


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


130 N.C. App. 692; 507 S.E.2d 42; 1998 N.C. App. LEXIS 1157


January 6, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 15, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 6 December 1996 by Judge F. Fetzer Mills in Forsyth County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Find no error in trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the eight indictments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Forsyth County (North Carolina), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of first-degree sexual offense with a minor and taking indecent liberties with a child, in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-27.4(a)(1) and 14-202.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with four counts of first-degree sexual offense and four counts of taking indecent liberties with his seven-year-old step-daughter. The indictments stated that the offenses were committed over a nine-month period. Defendant complained of the failure to state specific dates, but his motions to dismiss and for a bill of particulars were denied, although his attorney was allowed access to the prosecution's file. Defendant was convicted and he appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that defendant was informed with sufficient specificity of the charges against him, as required by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-924(a), especially since the prosecutor's file was opened for his attorney. A specific offense date was not an essential element of the crimes alleged and was not required to be included in the indictment in child sex abuse cases. Charging in the language of the applicable statutes was sufficient. Moreover, the offenses stated in §§ 14-27.4(a)(1) and 14-202.1 were not unconstitutionally void for vagueness, but were described with reasonable specificity to permit a person of ordinary intelligence to know that sexual conduct with a minor was proscribed.


OUTCOME: The convictions for first-degree statutory sexual offense and taking indecent liberties with a child were affirmed.

Jackson by & Through Robinson v. A Woman's Choice, Inc.


NO. COA97-1281


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


130 N.C. App. 590; 503 S.E.2d 422; 1998 N.C. App. LEXIS 1011


May 11, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 18, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiffs from order entered 8 September 1997 by Judge Abraham Penn Jones in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents brought an action against defendants alleging intentional or negligent infliction of emotional distress upon them and their daughter in performing an abortion upon the daughter. The Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) granted defendants' motions to dismiss, denied plaintiffs' motion for partial summary judgment, and declared moot plaintiffs' motion to strike certain affirmative defenses. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the trial court erred in concluding defendants acted in compliance with the provisions of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 90-21.7 (1995) because there was neither consent by plaintiffs nor judicial consent for the abortion that was performed by defendants. The court concluded that the trial court correctly determined as a matter of law that no violation occurred. The court held that where defendants were presented with an apparently valid written parental consent and were deceived into performing the abortion procedure upon the daughter, the unknowing and unintentional failure to obtain actual parental consent was not a violation of § 90-21.7. The court reviewed the statute and declined to adopt a strict liability interpretation. The court's decision rendered plaintiffs' motion to strike certain of defendants' affirmative defenses moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order dismissing plaintiffs' complaint.

 

883 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. McClendon


NO. COA97-863


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


130 N.C. App. 368; 502 S.E.2d 902; 1998 N.C. App. LEXIS 936


April 2, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 4, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 14, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 14 October 1996 by Judge Thomas W. Ross in Guilford County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which denied his motion to suppress evidence. Defendant pleaded guilty to charges of trafficking and conspiracy to traffic by transporting and possessing more than 50 pounds but less than 100 pounds of marijuana pursuant to a plea agreement in which he reserved the right to appeal the denial of his suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the stop of his vehicle, under the pretext of a traffic offense, was in violation of his constitutional rights, and that even if the initial stop was not unreasonable, the continued restrictions on his departure were beyond the scope of the traffic stop. The court held that: (1) defendant had been traveling in excess of the posted speed limit and was following another vehicle too closely, which provided probable cause for the police officer to stop his vehicle; thus, the stop was not inconsistent with the Fourth Amendment; (2) the police officer's initial investigation of defendant was reasonably related to the issuance of a warning ticket for speeding and following too closely and did not exceed the permissible scope of his investigation; (3) the officer's questioning was legitimately aimed at confirming defendant's identity in light of the fact that he was unable to produce the vehicle's registration and was unable to identify the owner of the vehicle; and (4) the detention of defendant beyond the issuance of the ticket was justified and was not unconstitutional because the officer had a reasonable suspicion that defendant was engaged in criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied defendant's motion to suppress.

 

884 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Schimmeck v. City of Winston-Salem


NO. COA97-1311


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


130 N.C. App. 471; 502 S.E.2d 909; 1998 N.C. App. LEXIS 947


May 14, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiffs from order entered 15 August 1997 by Judge Peter M. McHugh in Forsyth County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff government employee's action against defendant city, contending that the city's refusal to pay him retirement benefits was wrongful on several grounds, the employee appealed from the judgment of the Forsyth County Superior Court, which granted the city's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a police officer, injured his knee in the line of duty. He then reinjured his knee while on the way to work, and he was unable to perform as a sworn police officer. The employee did not receive a benefits award under the city's plan. Instead, the city offered him a position as a communications officer at his current rate of pay. The employee declined the position and retired. The employee brought an action for damages. The trial court granted summary judgment to the city. The court affirmed the judgment and held that because the existence of a contractual obligation was not present, summary judgment was properly granted. A person only became vested in a retirement plan upon satisfying the preconditions to the receipt of benefits. The plain language of the city's statute required five years of service before a member was entitled to permanent disability retirement. The employee did not have five years of service at the time of the amendments to the statute, his injury, or the submission of his application for disability. As such, his rights had not vested and there was no contractual obligation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city in an action by the employee for the city's refusal to have paid him retirement benefits.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff invitee appealed from an order of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant corporation in the invitee's negligence action seeking to recover for injuries she suffered during a parasailing accident.


OVERVIEW: While she was parasailing on a lake created by a hydroelectric dam operated by the corporation, the invitee was injured when she hit the top deck of a two-story pier. The corporation had licensed and sanctioned the renovations to the pier and licensed the pier on a yearly basis. The invitee filed a negligence action against the corporation, and the corporation filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the license held by the corporation did not confer upon it any affirmative duty to the invitee and that the corporation had no duty to warn the invitee of the pier because it was an obvious hazard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the corporation summary judgment in the invitee's negligence action.

Redevelopment Comm'n v. Johnson

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendants Andrew R. Johnson and Diane B. Johnson from order entered 1 May 1997 by Judge H. W. Butch Zimmerman in Guilford County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners sought review of a judgment from the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which found in favor of plaintiff Redevelopment Commission in their condemnation action pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-503(2) (1994).


OVERVIEW: The Commission brought a condemnation action to acquire vacant property that belonged to the landowners pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-503(2) (1994), which allowed the Commission to acquire through condemnation properties located in a "blighted or a rehabilitation area" for purposes of urban renewal. The landowners responded that the Commission abused their discretion in condemning the property without giving them an equal opportunity with other landowners to redevelop their properties consistent with the redevelopment plan, but the trial court found in favor of the Commission. The court found that where legislation granted the power of condemnation, discretion lied with the condemning authority to choose which property they sought to acquire through such means. The court noted that the landowners had offered no evidence of their proposed redevelopment plan for the condemned lots, therefore the Commission was found not to have abused its discretion nor acted arbitrarily or capriciously and their acquisition of the "blighted property" by condemnation was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the Commission in their condemnation action against the landowners.

Mark IV Bev., Inc. v. Molson Breweries USA, Inc.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beer wholesaler filed an action against defendants, supplier and alternate wholesaler, for violating certain laws and for unfair trade practices. The Rockingham County Superior Court (North Carolina), found in favor of the wholesaler. The supplier and the alternate wholesaler appealed.


OVERVIEW: The beer wholesaler contracted with the supplier to distribute a certain "brand" of beers. After the contract was signed, the supplier developed another beer. When it granted the distribution rights to the alternate wholesaler, the beer wholesaler filed an action complaining of a violation of the North Carolina Beer Franchise Law and of unfair trade practices. The supplier and the alternate wholesaler appealed. The court determined that (1) the law did not prohibit an injunctive action by one wholesaler against another; (2) the alternate wholesaler failed to preserve his complaint that the beer wholesaler failed to state a cause of action; and (3) the trial court correctly construed the term "brand" to encompass a common identifying trade name and that such construction of the North Carolina Beer Franchise Law did not render it unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the trial court that the beer wholesaler was entitled to the distribution rights to the new beer label.

Onslow County v. Moore


NO. COA97-32, NO. COA97-33, NO. COA97-35


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


129 N.C. App. 376; 499 S.E.2d 780; 1998 N.C. App. LEXIS 554


March 19, 1998, Heard in the Court of Appeals on remand  
May 5, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant in case No. 95 CvS 2836 from order entered 3 July 1996 by Judge W. Allen Cobb, Jr., in Onslow County Superior Court. Appeal by plaintiff and defendant in case No. 94 CvS 1980 from judgment entered 3 July 1996 by Judge W. Allen Cobb, Jr., in Onslow County Superior Court. Appeal by plaintiff and defendant in case No. 94 CVS 1981 from judgment entered 3 July 1996 by Judge W. Allen Cobb, Jr., in Onslow County Superior Court. The appeals were consolidated and originally heard in the Court of Appeals 16 September 1997. This Court dismissed the appeals for violations of the Rules of Appellate Procedure on 21 October 1997. 127 N.C. App. 546, 491 S.E.2d 670 (1997). In an order dated 5 March 1998, the SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA vacated the decision of the Court of Appeals and remanded the case to the Court of Appeals for consideration on the merits.



DISPOSITION: Case Nos. 94 CvS 1980 and 1981 are affirmed. Case No. 95 CvS 2836 is reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendant adult business owners challenged separate orders from the Onslow County Superior Court (North Carolina), which enjoined them from operating their businesses within 1,000 feet of certain facilities in violation of a county ordinance. They also appealed the dismissal of their complaints against plaintiff county alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional. A third defendant appealed a contempt order against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendants each owned adult businesses in violation of a county ordinance that prohibited sexually-oriented business from operating with 1,000 feet of a residence, house of worship, public school or playground, or other adult business. Two defendants filed an action against the county, alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The county obtained an injunction against them, prohibiting them from operating their businesses. The county obtained an injunction against the third defendant, and, after he failed to comply with the injunction, a contempt order was entered against him. On appeal, the court ruled that the failure of the county to adopt a county-wide comprehensive zoning plan did not preclude the county from regulating the location of adult and sexually-oriented businesses pursuant to its police powers. Because it did not impose an impermissible restraint on the freedom of expression, the court found that the ordinance was not in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I. The court also ruled that the lower court erred in including conduct of the third defendant that occurred prior to the time the injunction was "in force" against him in its contempt order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders from the lower court that enjoined two defendants from operating their adult businesses in violation of the county ordinance and also affirmed the constitutionality of the ordinance. The court reversed the order that held the third defendant in contempt for violation of his injunction and remanded to the trial court for entry of a new order.
