Hicks v. Leviton Mfg. Co.


No. COA94-1228


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


121 N.C. App. 453; 466 S.E.2d 78; 1996 N.C. App. LEXIS 68


August 30, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
February 6, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Industrial Commission I.C. No. 662453. Appeal by plaintiff from Opinion and Award of the North Carolina Industrial Commission entered 27 June 1994.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed an award from the North Carolina Industrial Commission, which held that she was entitled to reasonable medical treatment for her lung disease, incurred from working at defendant employer's facility, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-61.5, but that she was not entitled to additional compensation for subsequent lung damage that did not result in incapacity to work or loss of wages.


OVERVIEW: The employee was exposed to silica dust at her employer's facility and suffered from lung disease. The employee accepted benefits under § 97-61.5 for treatment of silicosis. The employee claimed that she was later exposed to ceramic dust that caused her to suffer permanent lung damage even though she did not sustain actual incapacity to work or loss of wages. The Commission found that the employee was not entitled to additional compensation under § 97-31(24) because that section provided that compensation was in lieu of all other compensation, and employee had already received compensation under § 97-61.5. On appeal, the court reversed and held that: (1) the employee's acceptance of benefits under § 97-61.5 did not preclude her from obtaining an award under § 97-31(24); (2) the employee was eligible for compensation under § 97-31(24) if she contracted lung disease other than asbestosis or silicosis that resulted in partial loss of her lungs but did not cause a loss of her wage-earning ability; and (3) if the employee's permanent injury was due to her occupational silicosis, she was entitled to elect between an award under § 97-31(24) or her previous award under § 97-61.5.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commission's award and remanded the case to the Commission for a determination of whether the employee was entitled to an award of compensation for permanent injury to her lungs due to occupational silicosis, and that if so, the employee was entitled to elect between such award and her previous award.

In re Robinson


No. COA94-1262


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


120 N.C. App. 874; 464 S.E.2d 86; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 950


September 11, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
November 21, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mecklenburg County. No. 93-J-721. Appeal by the State from order entered 29 September 1994 by Judge William G. Jones in Mecklenburg County District Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision from the Mecklenburg County District Court (North Carolina), which denied a transfer hearing and ruled that defendat juvenile's case could not be transferred pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. 7A-667(2), because he had not fully lived 13 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was born at 10:45 p.m. on August 22, 1981, was charged with a criminal offense allegedly occurring at 3:00 a.m. on August 22, 1994. Defendant moved to prohibit transfer of his case to the superior court and the trial court granted the motion because defendant had "not fully lived 13 years." The state appealed. The court determined that although the state had no appeal of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-667(2) (1989), the appeal would be treated a petition for writ of certiorari. The court determined that because the law did not recognize the fraction of a day in the computation of birthdays and because fractions of a day could no longer be considered when a juvenile could be transferred to superior court pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-608, the court erred in denying the transfer hearing and ruling that the juvenile could not be transferred. The court noted that the application of the "birthday rule" meant that for purpose of transfer, defendant became 13 at the first moment of the date of his birth. The order of the trial court was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court, which had denied the transfer hearing and ruled that defendant could not be transferred to superior court for trial, was reversed and remanded.

Garrett v. Winfree


No. 9418SC452


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


120 N.C. App. 689; 463 S.E.2d 411; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 904


February 2, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
November 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County No. 93 CVS 1832. Appeal by plaintiff from Order entered 24 January 1994 by Judge Thomas W. Seay, Jr. in Guilford County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sought review of a decision of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which entered judgment on the pleadings, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 12(c), in favor of defendant attorneys and dismissed the client's action for legal malpractice arising out of the attorneys' representation of the client in a workers' compensation case.


OVERVIEW: One of the attorneys assisted the client in obtaining permanent partial disability benefits after a work-related injury. Over the years, the client's medical condition worsened requiring amputation of both legs. Several years later, the client consulted the same attorneys on different occasions to file additional claims. The Industrial Commission refused to re-open the client's case because of the two-year limitations period, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97-47. The present malpractice action ensued, and the court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the claim because any cause of action was barred by the two-year statutes of limitations and repose under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-15(c) (1983). The court found that an action based upon the first allegation of a continuing duty to submit a change of condition began to accrue at the time the client received his last benefit payment, and, as to the second allegation for the re-opening of the claim, there was nothing that any attorney could have done to have avoided the limitations period. Thus, a judgment on the pleadings was proper. The court further found that § 1-15 was constitutional as applied under the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the attorneys' motion for a judgment on the pleadings and dismissing the client's legal malpractice action.

Caswell County v. Hanks


No. COA94-802


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


120 N.C. App. 489; 462 S.E.2d 841; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 884


August 28, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
October 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Caswell County No. 93 CVS 0152. Appeal by defendants from order entered 25 February 1994 by Judge Anthony M. Brannon in Caswell County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pet owners appealed an order from the Caswell County Superior Court (North Carolina), which sustained plaintiff municipal authority's determination under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 67-4.1(c) (1994) that the pet owners' dog was potentially dangerous.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 67-4.1(c), the municipal authority determined that the pet owners' dog was potentially dangerous. The pet owners appealed the finding, and following a de novo review of the record, the lower court sustained the municipal authority's decision. On appeal, the court remanded the case, holding that the lower court erred by conducting only a de novo review of the existing record rather than a de novo hearing. The court determined that the plain language of § 67-4.1(c) required the lower court to hear the case on its merit from beginning to end as if no hearing had been held by the municipal authority and without any presumption in favor of the municipal authority's decision. The court also held that the definition of "potentially dangerous dog" as set forth in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 67-4.1(a)(2)(c) (1994) was neither unconstitutionally vague nor overbroad because the case did not concern an area where the state sought to invade an area of protected freedoms and the statute provided sufficient notice for the pet owners and others to determine what conduct was proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court remanded a decision sustaining the municipal authority's determination that the pet owners' dog was potentially dangerous and directed the lower court to conduct a de novo hearing.

North Carolina Council of Churches v. State


No. 9310SC1162


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


120 N.C. App. 84; 461 S.E.2d 354; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 694


April 5, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
September 5, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County No. 92-CVS-10739. Appeal by plaintiffs from order filed 12 August 1993 by Judge Donald W. Stephens in Wake County Superior Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, death penalty opponents, appealed the order of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which granted summary judgment to defendants, state and corrections department, in their action for declaratory and injunctive relief to gain access to the grassy knoll outside a prison during an execution. They also appealed the orders that denied their N.C. R. Civ. P. 56(f) motion and their motion to amend the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The death penalty opponents were denied a permit to conduct a vigil on the grassy knoll outside a prison during an execution. However, death penalty proponents obtained a permit to stage a demonstration on a right of way during the same execution. The death penalty opponents filed an action and alleged free speech violations and viewpoint discrimination. The trial court denied the death penalty opponents' N.C. R. Civ. P. 56(f) motion and granted summary judgment for the state and the corrections department. The trial court also denied the motion to amend their complaint. This appeal followed. The court affirmed the orders. Although this case was moot, it was not dismissed because it was capable of repetition yet evaded review. Because the grassy knoll was not a public forum, reasonable, view-point-neutral restrictions on expressive conduct were allowed. Based on past disturbances and given the need for prison security, the permit was reasonably denied. The death penalty opponents neither alleged nor offered evidence of affirmative acts of viewpoint discrimination. There was no abuse of discretion in denying the Rule 56(f) motion or the motion to amend their complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that granted summary judgment for the state and the corrections department and denied the death penalty opponents' motions.

Appalachian Poster Advertising Co. v. Harrington


No. 9410SC477


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


120 N.C. App. 72; 460 S.E.2d 887; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 700


February 2, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
September 5, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County No. 86 CVS 0440. Appeal by petitioner from judgment and order entered 13 December 1993 by Judge Henry W. Hight, Jr., in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner advertising company appealed the judgment of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which affirmed respondent Secretary of Transportation of the State of North Carolina's (secretary) revocation of a roadside sign permit issued to the advertising company under the Outdoor Advertising Control Act (OACA).


OVERVIEW: The North Carolina Department of Transportation (department) issued an outdoor advertising permit to the advertising company for a nonconforming, pre-existing use. The advertising company changed the sign's message, poles, and distance from the highway. The district engineer notified the advertising company that the sign permit had been revoked because of OACA violations. The secretary affirmed the revocation. The trial court upheld the decision. On remand, the trial court again found for the secretary. The court reversed. The court examined N.C. Gen. Stat. § 136-130 (1993) and found it was the only source of authority for the enactment of rules and regulations with respect to outdoor signs. The court found that § 136-130 revealed that the advertising company's sign was not included in those signs that could be regulated by the department. The department only had the authority under the OACA to acquire by purchase, gift, or condemnation the advertising company's nonconforming, pre-existing sign, and did not have the authority to require removal of the advertising company's billboard pursuant to § 136-130 without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that affirmed the department's revocation of the advertising company's permit.

Southminster, Inc. v. Justus


No. COA94-763

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mecklenburg County No. 90-CVS-11666. Mecklenburg County No. 90-CVS-17819 Appeal by plaintiffs and defendant from judgment entered 29 March 1994 by Judge Shirley L. Fulton in Mecklenburg County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporations, religiously affiliated nonprofit care facilities for the elderly, appealed a decision of the Mecklenburg County Superior Court (North Carolina), which denied them exemption status as charitable or religious institutions for the payment of sales and use taxes under N.C Gen. Stat. § 105-164.14(b). Defendant revenue department appealed the award of refunds to the corporations based on a finding of constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: The corporations filed suit for refunds of sales and use taxes, but the department denied the exemptions, finding that the corporations were not charitable or religious institutions. The trial court concluded that the department's arbitrary, inconsistent, and inequitable application of the "'charitable and religious" test to allow exemptions for some, but not all institutions was discriminatory and unconstitutionally vague, violating the corporations' equal protection and due process rights. On review, the court modified and affirmed. The trial court erred in finding they were not charitable organizations. Thus, the corporations were entitled to refunds of the sales and use taxes paid.


OUTCOME: Modifying and affirming the judgment, the court ordered the department to pay refunds of sales and use taxes to the corporations.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina) that convicted him of multiple counts of first-degree rape, first degree sexual offense, first degree kidnapping, and one count of second-degree sexual offense and robbery. Defendant also appealed from the 14 consecutive life sentences imposed for the rape and sexual offenses and the concurrent 40-year and 10-year sentences for kidnapping and robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for rape, sexual offenses, kidnapping and robbery and his 14 consecutive life sentences and concurrent sentences for kidnapping and robbery. The court found that the trial court properly instructed the jury regarding serious personal injury within the meaning of N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-27.22(b), 14-27.42(b) and did not use improper factors in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first-degree rapes, first-degree and second-degree sexual offenses, kidnapping and robbery and the 14 consecutive life sentences for the rapes and sexual offenses as well as the concurrent 40-year term for kidnapping and the concurrent 10-year term for robbery.

Soles v. City of Raleigh Civil Serv. Comm'n


No. 9310SC235


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


119 N.C. App. 88; 457 S.E.2d 746; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 405


January 6, 1994, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
June 6, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County No. 91 CVS 10773. Appeal by intervenor from judgment entered 21 December 1992 by Judge W. Stephen Allen, Sr. in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city as intervenor challenged the judgment of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which found that the Raleigh Civil Service Act, Rule .0504, was unconstitutional in placing the burden upon petitioner employee for the city, to prove that the termination of his employment was "without justifiable cause." The trial court had remanded the cause to the Civil Service Commission (commission) for further proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The employee, an engineering aide for the city, was terminated from his employment under Raleigh, N.C., City of Raleigh Standard Procedure 300-14, Rev. B, § 4.2(k) (1984), which required a showing of "just cause" for termination of a city employee, for "personal conduct detrimental to city service." He sought an administrative hearing, alleging that he was "dismissed without justifiable cause," and the commission concluded that he failed to show by the greater weight of the evidence that he was terminated without justifiable cause under the Raleigh Civil Service Act, Rule .0504. On the employee's petition for review, the trial court held that Rule .0504 was unconstitutional in shifting the burden of proof to the employee and remanded to the commission. On appeal by the city, the court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) the employee had a constitutionally-protected property interest in retaining his position with the city; (2) as such, it could not deprive him of his job without due process; and (3) applying the Mathews three-factor balancing test, the employee had a right to retain constitutionally-protected employment until the city proved cause existed for termination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found that the rule placing the burden upon the employee to prove that the termination of his employment by the city was "without justifiable cause" was unconstitutional and which remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

945 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Eastern Appraisal Servs. v. State


No. 9410SC501


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


118 N.C. App. 692; 457 S.E.2d 312; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 379


January 26, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
May 16, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County No. 92 CVS 8416. Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 25 February 1994 by Judge Henry V. Barnette, Jr., in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer appealed an order from the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina) granting summary judgment in favor of defendants, Commissioner of Insurance of North Carolina and North Carolina Insurance Guaranty Association, and holding that they did not engage in an unconstitutional taking of the insurer's property of claim files of the insureds.


OVERVIEW: After the insurer became insolvent, it was subject to an order of liquidation. The insurer contended that claim files were its personal property developed by its employees. The insurer alleged that defendants gained possession of and used the claim files, which enabled the association to avoid the time and expense of obtaining the information, and that the claim files lost their value after that use. The court affirmed the contested order of summary judgment. The court held that defendants did not take the insurer's property so as to qualify the insurer for just compensation pursuant to the United States and North Carolina Constitutions. The court found that defendants needed to review the files to ascertain which claims to pursue and to abandon, in the manner the insurer would have settled and prosecuted the claims. The court decided that the commissioner's request for custody constituted an ordinary exercise of police power to protect the general welfare. The court determined that the interference with the insurer's interest in the files was reasonable and temporary. The court held that the diminution in the value of the files directly resulted from the insurer's insolvency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order challenged by the insurer and that entered the summary judgment for defendants by finding that they did not engage in an unconstitutional taking of the files.

State v. Wilson


No. 931SC1277


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


118 N.C. App. 616; 456 S.E.2d 870; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 334


January 9, 1995, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
May 2, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Pasquotank County. 92 CRS 4296, 403. 92 CRS 4304, 4311. Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 26 January 1993 by Judge D. Marsh McLelland in Pasquotank County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: New trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Pasquotank County Superior Court (North Carolina), which affirmed her criminal convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal charges after a jury trial. On appeal, the court held that: 1) the state did not violate Brady by withholding favorable evidence until trial, as defense counsel was aware of the potentially exculpatory testimony by the indictment; 2) defendant's right to due process was denied when the trial court failed to conduct a review of certain privileged materials brought for in camera review; 3) the trial court erred in allowing the prosecutor to question defendant about her prior use of cocaine and marijuana because the evidence was irrelevant and inadmissible under N.C. R. Evid. 608(b). The error was prejudicial, as the case turned on the credibility of the witnesses, and the jury could possibly have reached a different verdict had the prejudicial evidence not been disallowed; 4) the prosecutor improperly argued a previously denied allegation as a proven fact, and the trial court erred in failing to intervene.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and ordered a new trial.

 

947 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morgan


COA94-1196


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


118 N.C. App. 461; 455 S.E.2d 490; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 235


March 20, 1995, Heard In The Court Of Appeals  
April 4, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Onslow County Nos. 91 CRS 22644-22647. Appeal by defendant from order entered 29 July 1994 by Judge James R. Strickland in Onslow County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Onslow County Superior Court (North Carolina) denying his motion for appropriate relief on the ground that his convictions for trafficking in cocaine by possession, a violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 90-95(h)(3)(a) (1993), and failure to pay excise tax on the cocaine, a violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 105-113.110(a), 105-113.106(3) (1992), constituted double jeopardy. The State filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion for appropriate relief because his convictions for trafficking in cocaine by possession and for failure to pay excise tax on the controlled substance constituted double jeopardy. He argued that the punishments imposed upon those convictions violated double jeopardy. The court denied the State's motion to dismiss. While the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for appropriate relief was reviewable only by writ of certiorari under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1422(c)(3) (1988), the court had the discretion to treat defendant's attempted appeal as a petition for a writ of certiorari. The court held that because the State sought to collect the drug excise tax from defendant in the same prosecution, successive criminal prosecutions were not an issue. Further, defendant's contention that the trial court imposed multiple punishments for the same offense was without merit. The State charged defendant with violating two distinct criminal statutes that required proof of different elements. Because neither of the crimes was a lesser-included offense of the other, the convictions failed to support a plea of double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Cobey v. Cook


No. 9430SC379


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


118 N.C. App. 70; 453 S.E.2d 553; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 74


January 12, 1995, Heard in the Court of Appeals

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cherokee County No. 93 CvS 12. Appeal by defendant from order entered 10 January 1994 by Judge James U. Downs in Cherokee County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant polluter sought review of a decision from the Macon County Superior Court (North Carolina) that granted the motion for summary judgment of plaintiff, the State of North Carolina (state), in an action to enforce a civil penalty assessed on the polluter for violations of the Sedimentation Pollution Control Act of 1973 (SPCA), N.C. Gen. Stat. § 113A-50 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The polluter filed a motion that the state's complaint be dismissed because it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, Rule 12(b)(6), and that the SPCA as applied to him was unconstitutional in that it violated the Fourth and Fourteenth Amendments. The trial court denied the polluter's motion to dismiss, held that the state was entitled to judgment as a matter of law, and granted summary judgment to the state. The polluter sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the complaint was sufficient to withstand the polluter's motion to dismiss. The court found that the polluter had received notice and assessment of the civil penalty and did not file a petition to contest within the time period allowed and further refused to pay the penalty. The court determined that the polluter's argument that the SPCA violated the Fourth and Fourteenth Amendments lacked merit. The court ruled that the authority to assess civil penalties pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 113A-65.1(a) was necessary to the enforcement of the SPCA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the polluter's affidavit in opposition to the state's motion for summary judgment failed to raise genuine issue of material facts, and that the state was entitled as a matter of law to the relief granted.

White v. North Carolina Dep't of Env't, Health & Natural Resources

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent North Carolina Department of Environment, Health, and Natural Resources (department) appealed an order of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which determined that the department's commission's order dismissing petitioner former employee was arbitrary and capricious.


OVERVIEW: In a hearing held by the commission, the former employee was discharged for willful and repeated misuse of state funds. The trial court determined that the commission's order dismissing the employee was arbitrary and capricious. The evidence showed that the former employee had charged a number of personal calls to a state credit card that he had been issued, in violation of state law. The former employee had been advised in a directory issued to state employees that misuse of the card was punishable by dismissal. The court found that there was substantial evidence before the commission to have supported its conclusion that the employee had willfully and repeatedly misused state funds. The court held that the commission's decision did not lack fair and careful consideration.

Edward Valves, Inc. v. Wake County


No. 9410SC290


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


117 N.C. App. 484; 451 S.E.2d 641; 1995 N.C. App. LEXIS 1


October 26, 1994, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 3, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 91 CVS 10507. Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 1 December 1993 by Judge Robert L. Farmer in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from an order entered in the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which granted summary judgment to defendant Wake County Assessor (assessor) on the taxpayer's challenge to the assessment of its intangible corporate assets. The taxpayer had appealed its real property assessment by the assessor to the Wake County Board of Equalization and Review, but was never given a hearing.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a manufacturing facility, sold all of its assets and was required by law to allocate the consideration paid for its purchased assets, including numerous engineering drawings, which were then placed on the taxpayer's balance sheet for the first time and on federal income tax records as business property in Wake County. Taxes were assessed on the drawings, resulting in a significant increase in the taxpayer's bill. The taxpayer challenged the assessment and the trial court granted summary judgment to the assessor. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that the assessor's methodology for taxing self-created intangible property was unconstitutional under both the federal and state constitutions and also violated N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-284(a) and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court noted that the method of taxation resulted in a disproportionate taxation on those businesses which had been the subject of asset sales because no county tax form at the time required a taxpayer to list its intangible property, but such property had to be listed on forms related to asset sales.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court granting summary judgment to the assessor and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Garren


No. 933OSC1029, No. 933OSC1034


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


117 N.C. App. 393; 451 S.E.2d 315; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 1253


June 7, 1994, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Jackson County. No. 93 CRS 0703. Jackson County. No. 92 CRS 2221. Appeal by the State from order entered 4 August 1993 in Jackson County Superior Court by Judge Julia V. Jones.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Jackson County Superior Court (North Carolina), which affirmed orders of the district court judge declaring Jackson County, N.C., Noise Ordinance art. I, § 1-1(b)(3) (1991) unconstitutional and dismissing charges brought against defendants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with the violation of a county noise ordinance. Defendants made motions to dismiss the charge and in the two separate cases the district court judge declared Jackson County, N.C., Noise Ordinance art. I, § 1-1(b)(3) (1991) unconstitutional and allowed defendants' motions to dismiss. The state appealed and the superior court affirmed. The state sought review and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that § 1-1(b)(3) was drafted too broadly to be upheld as constitutional. The constitutional infirmity of § 1-1(b)(3) did not require the entire noise ordinance to be declared unconstitutional because Jackson County, N.C., Noise Ordinance art. I, § 1-1(a) (1991) was constitutionally valid and separable from the remainder of the ordinance and could therefore be given effect. The partial unconstitutionality of the noise ordinance did not support the granting of defendants' motions to dismiss the charges, and the trial court erred in allowing their motions. The court held that § 1-1(a) remained a valid and enforceable ordinance, and the state was entitled to proceed with the prosecution of defendants under the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of defendants and remanded the case in order for the state to proceed with the prosecution of defendants under the constitutional section of the noise ordinance.

Fleet Nat'l Bank v. Raleigh Oaks Joint Venture


No. 9310SC1276


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


117 N.C. App. 387; 451 S.E.2d 325; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 1256


September 14, 1994, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County. No. 90 CVS 10099. Appeal by defendants from judgment entered 20 September 1993 by Judge Wiley F. Bowen in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagors sought review from a judgment of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which entered a judgment of foreclosure in favor of plaintiff trustee for the mortgagee.


OVERVIEW: The trustee obtained a foreclosure judgment against the mortgagors and after sale he obtained a deficiency judgment. The individual mortgagor contended that he was not liable for the deficiency because he had not been personally served pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 45-21-16. The record revealed that attempts to serve him by certified mail were made and that notice was also posted on the property, and, further, that he had actual notice of the hearing but did not appear or object to service. The court held that whether or not the trustee used reasonable and diligent efforts to personally serve him was irrelevant because he had actual knowledge of the foreclosure. Accordingly, he could not assert the defense of lack of service contained in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 45-21-16(b)(2) because the purpose of that defense was to insure notice and compliance with due process and those concerns were not in issue. The court concluded that the mortgagors were unable to assert the defense contained in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 45-21.36 even though they had shown that the lease was worth substantially more than the trustee's bid because that defense only applied to real estate, not leaseholds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of foreclosure and deficiency judgment obtained by the trustee against the mortgagors.

Cannon v. North Carolina State Bd. of Educ.


No. 9210SC1211


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


117 N.C. App. 399; 451 S.E.2d 302; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 1267


October 22, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 9, 1995. As Corrected March 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Wake County. No. 92 CVS 1694. Appeal by plaintiffs from order entered 18 September 1992 by Judge D.B. Herring, Jr. in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which found that their challenge to the constitutionality of 1991 N.C. Sess. Laws 767, §§ 2, 3 was moot. The superior court entered judgment in favor of defendants, the North Carolina Board of Education, the Durham County Board of Commissioners, the Durham City Board of Education, the Durham County Board of Education, and the Durham County Board of Elections.


OVERVIEW: After the merger of a school system was found unconstitutional, the North Carolina legislature enacted 1991 N.C. Sess. Laws 767, §§ 2, 3 in an attempt to cure the finding of unconstitutionality. When plaintiffs filed an action against defendants that alleged the statutes were unconstitutional and would violate their voting rights, the trial court found that the issue had been rendered moot. On appeal, the court reversed the determination of mootness, holding that because, under the ruling of the first trial court, the Durham merger plan violated N.C. Const. art. I, § 19, N.C. Const. art. IX, § 2, the new session laws were ineffective as curative statutes vis a vis the Durham school merger. The court noted that a retrospective law was valid where the North Carolina Legislature originally had authority to confer the power or to authorize the act. Because the merger had previously been found unconstitutional, the Legislature lacked the authority to enact legislation that would validate the merger.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

John R. Sexton & Co. v. Justus

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant North Carolina Department of Revenue appealed a judgment from the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which granted summary judgment for plaintiff corporation in an action brought by the corporation seeking a refund of a soft drink tax it paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was a food service distributor. The Department of Revenue assessed an excise tax against the corporation's soft drink sales pursuant to the Soft Drink Excise Tax Act. The corporation paid the tax under protest, claiming that it was entitled to a refund because its fruit and vegetable juice concentrated products were exempt from taxation, and registration of these products was not required. The Department of Revenue denied the corporation's request for a refund. The corporation brought an action seeking a refund. Both parties moved for summary judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the corporation. The Department of Revenue appealed, claiming that the concentrated products were not entitled to an exemption because they were not properly registered as required under the Act. The court ruled that the corporation was entitled to a refund of the excise tax paid where the Act exempted from taxation natural fruit and vegetable concentrates such as the kind found in the corporation's soft drinks, and the law did not clearly require registration of such concentrates during the relevant time period in which the corporation was assessed the excise tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Guilford County Dep't of Emergency Servs. v. Seaboard Chem. Corp.


No. 9318SC419


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


114 N.C. App. 1; 441 S.E.2d 177; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 268


February 2, 1994, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 15, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. 89 CvS 2759. Appeal by defendants from judgment entered 15 October 1992 in Guilford County Superior Court by Judge Howard R. Greeson, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation challenged a decision by the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which barred it's counterclaims against plaintiffs, county and agencies, for failing to petition for review under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 153A-340. The superior court also granted the county and agencies a permanent injunction, enjoining the corporation from using property as a hazardous or toxic waste storage facility until a permit was obtained.


OVERVIEW: The county and agencies filed suit against the corporation, alleging that the corporation was violating the county's Hazardous Waste Ordinance in operating a hazardous waste reclamation and recovery processing facility without a special permit. The corporation brought a counterclaim, asserting (1) taking of private property for public use without just compensation; (2) inverse condemnation under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 40A-51; (3) violation of due process; (4) equitable estoppel and laches; and (5) a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court found that the superior court properly held that the corporation lost its right to appeal the dismissal of its counterclaims because a proper notice of appeal was not filed under N.C. R. App. P. 3(d) (1993). But the court also rejected the county and agencies' argument that because the corporation failed to raise certain issues by certiorari pursuant to § 153A-340, they were estopped. The court found that such review did not encompass the adjudication of issues of the type raised, such as whether the denial of the special use permit constituted a taking, inverse condemnation or a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision in part and reversed in part, finding that the superior court erred in holding that the corporation's counterclaims were barred for failure to petition for writ of certiorari pursuant to statute. The court also held that the superior court did not err in determining that the county and agencies' actions did not constitute a taking or a § 1983 violation and in granting the permanent injunction.

Naegele Outdoor Advertising v. City of Winston-Salem


No. 9221SC1137


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


113 N.C. App. 758; 440 S.E.2d 842; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 202


October 7, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
March 1, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Forsyth County. No. 92CVS2873. Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 14 August 1992 by Judge James M. Webb in Forsyth County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff advertiser appealed a judgment of the Forsyth County Superior Court (North Carolina), which, in the advertiser's action against defendant city, granted the city's motion to dismiss on statute of limitations grounds pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6) (1990).


OVERVIEW: On April 15, 1985, the city adopted Winston-Salem, N.C., Code, § 25-12(f), a zoning ordinance that dealt with the regulation of signs. The advertiser was notified by the city that his signs were in nonconformance with the ordinance and were required to be removed by April 15, 1992. On April 22, 1992, the city notified the advertiser that it was still in violation of the zoning ordinance, and that criminal charges might be brought if the violation continued for as long as 10 days after receiving the letter. The advertiser filed an inverse condemnation action against the city seeking damages due to the enactment of the ordinance. The trial court dismissed the action under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1A-1, N.C. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6)(1990) as untimely. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the advertiser's cause of action accrued when the ordinance was adopted because, immediately upon enactment, the ordinance interfered in a clear, concrete fashion with the property's primary use. Thus, because the advertiser failed to bring an action within the applicable nine month statute of limitations under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-54.1, his claim was barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

In re Ezzell


No. 9318SC208


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


113 N.C. App. 388; 438 S.E.2d 482; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 13


December 7, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Guilford County. 92 M 50. Appeal by respondent from order entered 8 October 1992 in Guilford County Superior Court by Judge W. Douglas Albright.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant magistrate sought review of an order from the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which permanently removed him from office as a magistrate.


OVERVIEW: The magistrate was accused of sexual harassment. The matter was set for a public hearing. The trial court requested that the district attorney present the case against the magistrate. At the hearing, the magistrate was present and represented by counsel. The trial court concluded that the charges were true and that the magistrate's conduct constituted willful misconduct in office and ordered his removal from office. The magistrate questioned the legality of the district attorney's presence at his removal hearing. He also claimed that the evidence did not support the findings of fact and that he was denied due process because the trial judge was not an impartial decision maker. Upon review, the court found that the magistrate did not have standing to challenge the district attorney's presence because the court did not think that the trial court would have reached a different conclusion, had it appointed independent counsel. Thus, the magistrate was not prejudiced. The court found that the evidence supported the trial court's findings. The court concluded that there was no evidence of personal bias or prejudice on the part of the trial judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order permanently removing the magistrate from office.

Foreman v. Sholl

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

January 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Buncombe County. 90 CVS 1885. Appeal by plaintiffs from order entered 28 May 1992 in Buncombe County Superior Court by Judge Robert D. Lewis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from Buncombe County Superior Court (North Carolina), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, in plaintiff's action to quiet title.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-38 (1983), that they under known boundaries for more than seven years asserted continuous, open, notorious and hostile adverse possession of the premises in question under color of title and should thus be declared the owners in fee simple of the land. A group of defendants moved for summary judgment on the ground that plaintiffs had not exercised adverse possession under color of title because the deed upon which plaintiffs relied to establish color of title did not sufficiently describe the property purportedly conveyed. The defendants claimed to own the tracts of land described. The lower court entered judgment against plaintiffs on all of plaintiffs' claims. The court affirmed, finding that the cause of action was commenced more than three months before plaintiffs could have acquired an interest in the property by virtue of adverse possession, so the trial court correctly entered summary judgment on this basis. Additionally, defendants showed that plaintiffs could not prove an essential element of their claim, which was that the deed upon which plaintiffs relied contained an adequate description of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment against plaintiffs, in their action to quiet title.

Brantley v. Watson


No. 9210SC1008


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


113 N.C. App. 234; 438 S.E.2d 211; 1994 N.C. App. LEXIS 3


September 16, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
January 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Wake County. Nos. 92SP178, 91E1813. Appeal by petitioner from order entered 17 August 1992 by Judge Robert L. Farmer in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial judge is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband sought review of a judgment from the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which upheld the validity of a postnuptial agreement between the husband and his deceased wife and which rejected the husband's claim to a year's allowance under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 30-15 (1984). The husband claimed that the agreement was invalid because it failed to comply with N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-6, 52-10.


OVERVIEW: The husband and the wife executed a postnuptial agreement whereby each released, renounced, and quitclaimed any and all rights accorded to each of them under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 30-1 (1984), to dissent from the will of the other if surviving. The wife died, and thereafter, the husband filed a dissent from the wife's will and a petition for a year's allowance. In defense, respondents argued that the postnuptial agreement barred the husband's dissent and his application for a year's allowance. The trial court found for respondents, refusing to invalidate the postnuptial agreement for failing to comply with N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-6, 52-10. Thereafter, the husband sought review. In affirming, the court held that the agreement could not be set aside because of its noncompliance with N.C. Gen. Stat. § 52-10 and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 52-6, which required the wife's private examination, because the principle of equal protection under the law made gender-based discrimination presumptively unconstitutional. In reversing, the court held that the agreement, which referred only to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 30-1 (1984), did not forfeit the right to a year's allowance under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 30-15 (1984).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the validity of the postnuptial agreement but reversed the judgment rejecting the husband's claim to a year's allowance.

 

961 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


City of New Bern v. New Bern-Craven County Bd. of Educ.


No. 923SC730


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


113 N.C. App. 98; 437 S.E.2d 655; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1306


June 3, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
December 21, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Craven County. No. 88 CVS 1780. Appeal by defendants except for the Attorney General, and cross-appeal by plaintiff from order entered 24 February 1992, by Judge G. K. Butterfield in Craven County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county, the county's community college, and others, sought review of the judgment of the Craven County Superior Court, which ruled that three statutes that transferred exclusive jurisdiction over the enforcement of various building codes from plaintiff city to the county were unconstitutional. The city filed a cross-appeal against the trial court's order that its judgment would only operate prospectively.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the challenged legislation violated N.C. art. II § 24, which prohibited the general assembly from passing "local " or "special" acts. In asserting that the statutes were constitutional, defendants contended that in order to be prohibited such statutes had to directly effect health and sanitation, traditionally local concerns, they could not be merely tangentially related to such concerns. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the statutes in question were in local in nature and that they were constitutionally prohibited subjects of legislation. Whether the analysis was made under the McIntyre "reasonable classification" test or the Emerald Isle test of "general public interest," the acts were local. The legislation served to strip the power of city inspectors to enforce the state building code, a purpose that was directly related to health and sanitation. The general assembly had singled out certain units of local government for special treatment. There was no rational basis for separating such governmental units and imposing a transfer of jurisdiction over the enforcement of building codes from the city to the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Hodge


No. 9210SC1286


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


112 N.C. App. 462; 436 S.E.2d 251; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1124


September 28, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 8, 1993. Second Correction February 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Nos. 91 CRS 85692, 92 CRS 6647. Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 2 September 1992 by Judge F. Gordon Battle in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of felonious possession of cocaine and denied his motion to dismiss the habitual felon indictment.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant's possession of cocaine paraphernalia, the location of the cocaine beneath defendant's body, and his statements that he bought the cocaine so that he could have gotten high were substantial incriminating circumstances from which defendant's constructive possession of the cocaine could have been inferred, and therefore the trial court did not err when it denied his motion to dismiss the charge of felonious possession of cocaine. The court further held that there was no error in the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the habitual felon indictment because the indictment complied with N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-7.3. The court determined that the Habitual Felon Act, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-7.1, was not unconstitutional and did not deny defendant due process or equal protection of the law nor did it subject him to double jeopardy. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not err when it admitted into evidence certain documents that the prosecution used to show that defendant was actually the defendant in the present matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied defendant's motions to dismiss the charge of felonious possession of cocaine and to dismiss the habitual felon indictment.

House of Raeford Farms v. City of Raeford


No. 9216SC1118


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


112 N.C. App. 522; 435 S.E.2d 829; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1134


October 6, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 90-CVS-398. Appeal by plaintiff from judgments entered 22 July 1992 and 31 August 1992 in Hoke County Superior Court by Judge B. Craig Ellis.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the owners of a turkey slaughtering farm, sought review of the judgment of the Hoke County Superior Court (North Carolina), which dismissed the operators' petition for writ of certiorari to review penalties and costs assessed against the operators by respondent, the City of Raeford.


OVERVIEW: The City issued a show cause order to the owners, regarding its previous notice of noncompliance to the owners. The order stated that the owners had 15 days to request a hearing before a superintendent to show cause why the owners' permit should not be revoked. At a hearing on the matter, the hearing offer assessed penalties and enforcement costs against the owners, and further ordered that the owners pay the sums within five days or have their permit revoked. On appeal, the issue was whether the City could assess penalties and costs against the owners where the notice for the hearing was solely for the owners to present evidence to show cause why its permit to discharge wastewater should not be revoked. The court found that based upon the City's show cause order, there was nothing to indicate that any matters besides the decision to revoke or not to revoke the owners' permit was to be argued at the show cause hearing. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment, with directions for the trial court to enter an order vacating the City's assessment of penalties and costs, because the City did not have authority to assess penalties and costs at a show cause hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment for entry of an order vacating the City's assessment of penalties and costs.

State v. Smith

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


112 N.C. App. 512; 436 S.E.2d 160; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1138

November 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No 89 CRS 77510. Appeal by defendant from judgment and commitment entered 23 September 1992 by Judge Wiley F. Bowen in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to sell and deliver and as a habitual felon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine and the jury found defendant guilty of being a habitual felon. Defendant sought review and asserted that the trial court had erred in its denial of his motion to dismiss the habitual felon indictment because the indictment failed to comply with the statutory requirement of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-7.3. The court stated that although the habitual defender indictment was labeled as part B with the indictment for cocaine possession labeled as part A, the record revealed that they were separate indictments. The court stated that the indictment gave the date in which defendant had pleaded guilty for the prior conviction rather than the date he had pleaded guilty and that that was sufficient to have given him notice of the prior felony conviction that was to be used against him to convict him as a habitual felon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to sell and deliver and his conviction as a habitual felon.

In re Appeal of Barbour


No. 9210PTC570


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


112 N.C. App. 368; 436 S.E.2d 169; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1120


April 29, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
November 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 87PTC239. Appeal by Joe Barbour from a decision of the Property Tax Commission entered 23 January 1992 affirming the decision of the Alamance County Board of Commissioners.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board member appealed a decision of the Property Tax Commission (North Carolina), which affirmed a decision granting a property tax exclusion to a retirement group pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32).


OVERVIEW: The Alamance County Board of Commissioners granted a property tax exclusion to a retirement group related to a denominational ministries program. A member of the board challenged the decision, alleging that the group had failed to meet the exemption requirements and arguing that the statute discriminated against residential property owners who were not exempt from taxation. The decision was affirmed, and the board member appealed. The court affirmed, holding that promoting the safety and welfare of the aged or infirm was a legitimate state objective and that the exemption had some rational relationship to that legitimate state interest. The classification of homes for the aged, sick, or infirm was set up to compensate for the loss of their tax exempt status as charitable institutions by the statute, and the distinction was neither arbitrary or capricious, as required to prove a discrimination claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that a retirement group related to a denominational ministries program was entitled to a property tax exemption under the statute in an action by a board member that alleged the group did not meet the exemption requirements.

State ex rel. Utilities Comm'n v. Empire Power Co.


No. 9210UC724


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


112 N.C. App. 265; 435 S.E.2d 553; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1092


May 28, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 19, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Docket No. SP-91. Appeal by petitioner from order entered 23 April 1992, by the North Carolina Utilities Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner power company sought review from an order entered by the North Carolina Utilities Commission (commission), which dismissed the power company's petition for a Certificate of Public Convenience and Necessity (CPCN). A number of related power and light companies entered the action as intervenors. The power company contended that that the commission's dismissal of the CPCN exceeded constitutional and legislative limits.


OVERVIEW: The commission dismissed an application by the power company for a Certificate of Public Convenience and Necessity (CPCN) and the power company appealed. Upon review, the court affirmed the commission's decision. The court ruled that the commission was entitled to resort to other parts of Chapter 62 for the processing of applications for CPCN, other than those found in N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 62-82, 62-220.1 (1989), in order to effectuate the purpose of the chapter, which was to promote the policy of the state. The court held that the commission's establishment of minimum filing requirements did not constitute an unconstitutional exercise of legislative powers and that the standard of public convenience and necessity, coupled with the policies of the state, were sufficient to guide the commission in deciding a CPCN case. Further, the court stated that the legislature's delegation of that authority was not unconstitutional. The court ruled that the language in § 62-82 was directory and thus not jurisdictional, and that the commission's dismissal was a proper exercise of its authority. Finally, the court noted that the power company had the right to file a future CPCN application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's dismissal of the power company's application for a Certificate of Public Convenience and Necessity.

 

967 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pendleton


No. 9211SC880


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


112 N.C. App. 171; 435 S.E.2d 100; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 1066


June 14, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
October 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 91 CRS 3735. Appeal by the State from order entered 29 April 1992 by Judge Steve Allen in Harnett County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State challenged the decision of the Harnett County Superior Court (North Carolina), which entered judgment in favor of appellee complainant finding a state constitutional provision unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The complainant argued that the effect of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 74A was to advance the religious principles of a university. He contended that when campus police enforced the university's rules of conduct they were exercising authority granted by the State under § 74A which created an appearance of State endorsement of the university's religious beliefs and practices. On review, the court reversed. The court found nothing in § 74A that evinced an intent to aid, promote, restrict, hinder, or otherwise affect any religion or any religious organization. The statute made no distinction between religious and secular institutions, and any aid received by the university was indirect. The court held that the primary effect of § 74A was neither to advance nor inhibit religion. The court also held that § 74A did not create an excessive entanglement between church and state. The statute's delegation of law enforcement authority did not violate the Establishment Clause. The court concluded that § 74A had a secular legislative purpose and it was not an unconstitutional delegation of the State's law enforcement authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Nissan Div. of Nissan Motor Corp. v. Nissan


No. 9210SC802


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


111 N.C. App. 748; 434 S.E.2d 224; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 932


June 15, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
September 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by plaintiff from order entered 6 April 1992 by Judge Donald H. Stephens in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff automobile manufacturer sought review of an order entered in the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant automobile dealer affirming a Department of Motor Vehicles hearing officer's decision that the automobile manufacturer had failed to give the automobile dealer proper notice of its opposition to the automobile dealer's relocation as required by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-305.


OVERVIEW: A Department of Motor Vehicles hearing officer reviewed the automobile manufacturer's refusal to approve the automobile dealer's relocation of its facilities under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-305 and determined that the automobile manufacturer had waived its opposition by failing to give written notice as required by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-305(4). The court reversed the summary judgment affirming the hearing officer's decision, ruling that the notice of objection which was delivered by a private delivery company rather than the United States Postal Service was registered mail within the meaning of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-305(4). The court also ruled that the trial court did not retroactively apply the amended version of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 20-305 so as to deprive the automobile manufacturer of its vested rights to control the location of its dealership, and that the statute, as amended, did not unconstitutionally impair the automobile manufacturer's right to control the location of its dealerships because the statute was a reasonable exercise of the state's police power under the Contracts Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment entered in favor of the automobile dealer which affirmed a determination of a Department of Motor Vehicles hearing officer that the automobile manufacturer had failed to give the automobile dealer proper notice of its objection to relocation and remanded the case for further proceedings.

In re Hayes


No. 9210SC792


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


111 N.C. App. 384; 432 S.E.2d 862; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 799


June 7, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
August 3, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by respondent from order entered 21 February 1992 by Judge Donald W. Stephens in Wake County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, who had been committed for treatment in 1989 after acquittal of murder by reason of insanity, appealed the order of the Wake County Superior Court (North Carolina), which directed respondent's continued commitment after a hearing held under N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 122C-268.1(i), 122C-276.1(c) (1991). Respondent argued that the statutes under which he was committed were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In 1989, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 122C, respondent was committed to a hospital for treatment after acquittal by reason of insanity of murder and related charges. In 1991, § 122C was amended, shifting the burden of proof at recommitment hearings from the state to a respondent to show lack of mental illness requiring confinement and providing lesser procedural protections than those given in civil commitments. In 1992, respondent was ordered recommitted after a hearing held under the amended statutory guidelines. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's determination. The court held that the amended statute violated neither the Due Process nor the Equal Protection Clauses of the federal or state constitutions because respondent was given an adequate opportunity to be heard, and because one committed as an insanity acquittee, since he or she raised the defense in the first place, was entitled to fewer procedural protections than involuntary civil committees. The court also held that the amended statute was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law because it was strictly a procedural change which neither altered a definition of an offense, nor increased the punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's 1992 recommitment of respondent under the procedures and guidelines of the amended statute.

Fogleman v. D&J Equip. Rental, Inc.


No. 9218SC418


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


111 N.C. App. 228; 431 S.E.2d 849; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 706


March 30, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by A. A. Ryan Ornamental Iron, Inc. and Liberty Mutual Insurance Company from order entered 27 January 1992 in Guilford County Superior Court by Judge William H. Freeman.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, third party workers' compensation insurer (insurer), sought review of a judgment from the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina), which approved a settlement agreement between appellees, employee and his wife (employee), with a crane operator that prevented the insurer from seeking subrogation for amounts previously paid to the employee as workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a welder, was injured when he fell from a platform that was being raised by the crane operator in 1989. The insurer admitted workers' compensation liability and paid the employee compensation for temporary total disability and health care expense and for permanent partial disability. The employee filed a civil action against the crane operator for negligence. The crane operator and the employee reached a settlement agreement in 1992. The insurer did not participate in the settlement negotiations or agreement. The insurer sought an adjustment of its subrogation lien on the settlement funds. The superior court found that the insurer was not a party to the settlement agreement and ruled that it was not entitled to subrogation for the amount previously paid to the employee under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 97.10.2(j), N.C. R. Civ. P. 97.10.2(j) (1991). The insurer claimed on appeal that the superior court erroneously applied § 97.10.2(j) retroactively. The court agreed with the insurer's claim. The court ruled that the superior court's application of the amended version of § 97-10.2 deprived the insurer of vested rights and was unconstitutionally retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's approval of a settlement agreement between the employee and a crane operator that prevented the insurer from seeking subrogation for amounts previously paid to the employee as workers' compensation benefits and remanded the action for further proceedings.

State v. Minter


No. 9118SC1199


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


111 N.C. App. 40; 432 S.E.2d 146; 1993 N.C. App. LEXIS 707


March 1, 1993, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant from judgment entered 26 June 1991 in Guilford County Superior Court by Judge W. Douglas Albright.



DISPOSITION: New trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Guilford County Superior Court (North Carolina) convicting him for his involvement in a criminal conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his criminal conviction, defendant contended that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that they could find him guilty of conspiracy without limiting the conspiracy to one with the co-conspirator named in the indictment. It was also contended that the trial court erred in allowing the state to introduce, for impeachment purposes, the grand jury testimony of the alleged co-conspirator. The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. N.C. Const. art. I, § 23 provided that in all criminal prosecutions an accused had the right to be informed of the accusation against him. The challenged jury instruction unconstitutionally served to put defendant on trial for an offense additional to that named in the indictment. However, the challenged grand jury testimony was properly admitted. Once the alleged co-conspirator refused to testify for the prosecution, or claimed that parts of his earlier, sworn statements before the grand jury were false, the state's use of that grand jury testimony was proper for impeachment purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial.

McDonald's Corp. v. Dwyer


No. 913SC1171


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

November 30, 1992, Heard in the Court of Appeals  
July 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendants from order entered 22 October 1991 by Judge David E. Reid, Jr., in Craven County Superior Court.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, claimants to a disputed tract of land, appealed from an order entered by the Craven County Superior Court (North Carolina), which determined that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-44.2 was constitutional and that plaintiff adjacent landowner was entitled to possession of a portion of an abandoned railroad easement located adjacent to its property.


OVERVIEW: The adjacent landowner filed a complaint stating that it owned in fee simple and possessed a tract of land located adjacent to an abandoned railroad easement and requested to be declared the owner in fee simple of and entitled to a portion of the abandoned railroad easement. The trial court ruled in favor of the adjacent landowner. On appeal, the claimants contended that the adjacent landowner was not entitled to the property pursuant to § 1-44.2 because the statute was unconstitutional under the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution, as well as the North Carolina Constitution, in that it failed to provide notice or a hearing and effected the taking of land without just compensation. The court reversed, holding that § 1-44.2 was unconstitutional in its application to fee simple landowners who were in possession of disputed property because the statute failed to provide them with adequate notice, an opportunity to be heard, and with just compensation. The court concluded that the enactment of the statute was retroactive and affected the claimants' vested property rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision ruling that the statute was constitutional and that the adjacent landowner was entitled to possession of a portion of the abandoned railroad easement.
